Englishman Lincoln Goes to Europe to Promote Buddhism 116

To Build Buddhist Temples in Europe

The Da Mei Wan Bao [Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury] reports that Englishman Lincoln, Dharma name Chao Gong, a monk who has converted to Buddhism, arrived in Shanghai from the north and announced the purpose of his trip yesterday. He said he will go to Europe to promote Buddhism. If many people convert, he plans to raise funds in continental Europe to build Buddhist temples, hoping to transform the people with the true meaning of the Buddha's teachings. As for the rumor from Tianjin that he had disagreements with the monks of a certain temple in the north, it is completely untrue. All the Chinese monks and lay Buddhists he has met in his life have been kind, amiable, and loving like brothers. If he cannot fulfill his wishes on this trip to Europe, he will still live in seclusion and practice true cultivation, as Europeans seem to be preparing to brew war again, so it may not be time to promote Buddhist transformation yet.

Record of the Trial of Zhao Weixian, the Criminal in the Wei Tingrong Kidnapping Case 117

Zhao Presented a Letter of Appointment Requesting Bail, Which Was Not Approved

On the morning of July 24, 1929, at 10:50 AM, Wei Tingrong, manager of the Sino-French Bank and commander of the Chinese Volunteer Corps in the former French Concession, was traveling with his children in his own car to return home from the Sino-French Bank, which was parked on Zhu Bao San Road, when he was kidnapped. The car was driven to Xinkaihe, where the children and the driver were forced out of the car. The kidnappers drove the car, using sedatives on Wei, who passed out. The car went to Dongjiadu and he was taken by boat to the countryside in Nanhui, Pudong. He was imprisoned and extorted for 180,000 yuan for ransom to be negotiated in Hangzhou. Two months later, several kidnappers were arrested by the French police. After questioning, the French Public Concession sentenced them to imprisonment. Now, the special investigation department of the French police has arrested Cai Weicai (from Nanhui, Pudong) and Lv Mingwang (from Shaoxing). According to Lv and others, the case was masterminded by Wei's brother-in-law, Zhao Weixian. Cai and Lv were interrogated and detained by the Second Special District Court. Colleagues from the detective agency went to 3 Fuxing Bridge in Xumen, Suzhou, and arrested Zhao. He was transferred to Shanghai the day before yesterday and detained in the French police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Special Court for questioning. Zhao was wearing a white wool western suit, a monk's hairstyle, a gray straw hat, and leather shoes, looking energetic and calm. Judge Luo, accompanied by Prosecutor Ding Shikui, opened the court for interrogation. Feixi Zhen, a lawyer from the police station, explained the case and requested a postponement to be jointly tried with the arrested defendants. During the interrogation, Zhao Weixian confessed that he was 31 years old, from Chenzhou, Hunan, and is currently the commander of the Sixth Independent Battalion of the Water Police of the Ministry of Finance. The troops are stationed in Bengbu to protect the road. He was arrested while taking leave to return to Suzhou to visit relatives and friends. He knew nothing about Wei Tingrong's kidnapping and hired a lawyer to defend him. He presented the letters of appointment and photos of his previous and current positions as evidence. Judge Luo ordered the defendant to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing for the morning of the 28th of this month. After the order, the defendant's lawyer requested to allow the defendant to be released on bail. The court refused because the case was serious.

Murder for Property 118

The case occurred in Nanhui, but the death occurred in Shanghai

Qiu, a woman from Nanhui County, Pudong, who was 40 years old and ran a shoe store, adopted Mei as her husband. Qiu also had an older sister and a younger brother. Recently, Mei wanted to change Qiu's property deeds to the Mei surname, but Qiu refused. As a result, Mei harbored resentment and suddenly became murderous. On the evening of the 13th of this month, around 3:00 AM, Mei inserted an iron bar about several inches long and as thick as a little finger into Qiu's vagina and uterus, about two inches deep. Qiu fainted from the extreme pain. Later, family members discovered it and treated her at a local hospital, and reported to the local Public Security Bureau to arrest Mei. On the 18th, she was transferred to the Xiaoshadu Road Labor Hospital in Shanghai for treatment, but it was ineffective. She died on the 22nd due to serious injuries. The hospital reported to the Putuo Road police station, and ordered Chinese detectives to investigate. They then moved the body to the Ferry Road coroner's office. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Liu Chun, arrived at the office to examine the body. According to Zhang Qiu, the deceased was my sister. I live in Shanghai, so I did not witness the situation at the time. However, my brother-in-law also tried to stab my sister to death with a knife last year, but it did not happen. I have already reported Mei to the Public Security Bureau under the jurisdiction of Nanhui County, Pudong. Mr. Guo then ordered that the deceased Mei Qiu was indeed injured and died before her death. The body was handed over to Zhang Qiu to collect and coffin the body with a written guarantee.

Hua Shang Electric Company Worker Yang He Shang Dies Tragically from Electric Shock 119

The Company Has Provided Generous Compensation

Yang Heshang, a worker at the Hua Shang Electric Company, died from electric shock at 10:30 yesterday morning while repairing the No. 24 square compartment (i.e., the pressure receiving station). The details are as follows: Yang Heshang was 34 years old, from Wuxi, and has been working for the company for more than ten years. He usually worked very diligently. He married a woman named Zhang and had a son who is currently four years old. He lived in the worker dormitory of the Hua Shang Electric Company on Guohuo Road. Except for rest, he went to work at the company every day. Yesterday morning, the company received a report that the power line between Longhua and Xujiahui was damaged, and immediately sent foreman Ye Bingzhang and worker Yang Heshang to investigate and repair it. At around 10:00 AM, he went to find the damaged wire in the No. 24 square compartment of the west fort on Longhua Road and opened the power gate of the compartment. The over-motor for the 5,500-pound volt power supply was placed there. Because the power was sufficient, Yang Heshang was sucked in by the power when he pulled the power gate switch, and he fell to the ground after being electrocuted. Foreman Ye Bingzhang saw the worker being electrocuted and falling to the ground, and immediately reported to the company by telephone and immediately dispatched a car to transport the worker back to the company. First, a local method was used to rescue him by moving Yang's body to a ditch filled with Yin Ni and using mud and water to extinguish the electricity on his body. Because of the excessive electricity received and the long time, a Western doctor, Wu Lizhong, was asked to inject and rescue him, but it was ineffective. He was later sent to the Southwest Hospital for treatment, but he died at around 11:00 AM. After Yang's death, the local Bao reported to the local court for an inquest. The court dispatched Prosecutor Wu to the inquest at 5:00 PM yesterday. The autopsy found that he died from electric shock. He filled out the death certificate. The funeral arrangements are scheduled for 1:00 PM today for the wake and 3:00 PM for the funeral. All the company's workers and friends took a leave of absence early to attend the funeral. After the manager of the company, Lu Bohong, learned that the worker Yang Heshang had died in the line of duty due to his long service and hard work, he was given special treatment. According to the regulations of the labor union, the company allocated about 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses, severance pay, and condolence money. It is said that there is also a special condolence and resettlement fee, which is currently being negotiated by labor and management and will be allocated once it is finalized. Yesterday, the company first allocated 50 yuan to his wife for funeral expenses.

Joy Turns to Sorrow: A Patron Dies of Exhaustion 120

The Brothel Owner Secretly Replaces the Ugly Prostitute with the Dead Patron's First Choice

Liu Chunshan, from Yangzhou, runs a brothel at 208-209 Ziyou Lane on Wuma Road, housing five or six prostitutes. One of them, Xiao Ruyizi, picked up a stranger near Sima Road last night, a Jiangbei pimp about thirty years old. After the price was paid, they became guests in the boudoir, sharing a dream. Unexpectedly, joy turned to sorrow, and the patron died of exhaustion. The brothel owner was frightened and immediately reported to the police station. The police sent detectives to investigate and took Xiao Ruyizi to the police station. At the same time, the body was moved to the coroner's office on Ferry Road, awaiting an inquest this morning. However, according to neighbors, the prostitute who was taken away was not Xiao Ruyizi, who slept with the deceased. The brothel owner, to avoid thorough investigation, secretly replaced Xiao with Jin Xian, the ugliest prostitute, temporarily as a representative. Jin Xian was renamed Juhua, and claimed to the police that the prostitute was her own body, without a brothel owner. It is now reported that the police chief has learned the truth and will thoroughly investigate the matter.

Attempted Rape and Defilement of Qiu Afeng 121

Seventeen-Year-Old Woman Pimps; Twenty-Four-Year-Old Boat Hand Seeks Undue Advantage

Qiu Afeng, daughter of Qiu Daoxun of Xiangshan, residing in Gaojia Chang, Wusong, is twenty-two years old and of fair appearance, awaiting marriage. Around eight o'clock the night before last, a neighbor, Ji Wu's wife, went to call Afeng to play at her house. Unexpectedly, when Afeng arrived in Ji Wu's room, there was a man she did not know inside. Afeng immediately turned to leave, but Ji Wu's wife closed the door, preventing her from leaving. The man then stepped forward and embraced Afeng, attempting to violate her. Afeng, seeing this, was greatly frightened and cried out for help. At this critical moment, Afeng's younger brother happened to be passing by outside and, hearing his sister's urgent cries, quickly broke down the door and entered. The man took the opportunity to escape. Afeng and her brother then went home and told their father, Qiu Daoxun, who reported the incident to the police. Ji Wu's wife was arrested, and the man was captured in Lao's store on Dongsheng Road. Both were sent to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau. District Chief Zhao Ze Zhou interrogated them. Initially, Qiu Daoxun and Afeng recounted the events. Ji Wu's wife then stated that she was seventeen years old and from Dinghai, and that Qiu Afeng often played at her house. She claimed that her father's accusation of her being a pimp was a false accusation. The man claimed his name was Lin Ayu, twenty-four years old, from Zhenhai, working as a hand on a fishing boat. Around seven o'clock the night before last, the boat arrived at Wusong, and he went ashore, bringing old bamboo ropes from the boat to Ji Wu's house. He stated that he had thought of his cousin, Zheng Afeng, and asked Ji Wu to find her for a chat, but Ji Wu mistakenly called Qiu Afeng. Upon seeing her, he was very surprised and did not exchange a single word with Qiu Afeng. He claimed that her father's accusation of him molesting his daughter was entirely unjust. After reviewing the statements, District Chief Zhao deemed Lin Ayu and Ji Wu's wife to be extremely unlawful and, the following morning, dispatched police officers to escort them to the Public Security Bureau for legal action.

Wang Chunshun Dies Tragically 122

Run Over by Cart, Falls, and Dies

Investigation Reveals Prior Fight

Suspected Murderer Detained at District Office

Yesterday afternoon, a fatal incident occurred at the Wuzhen Bridge embankment in Zhabei. The deceased was a child from Yancheng named Wang Chunshun, fifteen years old, who earned a living by carrying a shoulder pole and shaving heads. Around three-thirty yesterday afternoon, Wang was playing with several companions by the roadside when a cart traveling from north to south crossed the bridge. Wang suddenly fell to the ground and did not get up. A police officer stationed at the bridge arrived upon hearing the news and, upon inspection, found that the child's head was bleeding and that he had already died. Suspecting that he had been run over by the cart, the officer took the cart driver, Qi Benxiang, Zhang Xingru, and five others, along with the cart, to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau for questioning. However, after investigating the injuries on Wang Chunshun's body, the bureau determined that they did not appear to have been caused by cart wheels. Furthermore, nearby residents claimed that Wang Chunshun had been fighting with several other children and was struck, resulting in his death. The bureau chief ordered detectives to summon the suspect, Liu Pinglin, along with his older brother, Liu Kunlin, and Shi Xiaguangsheng, for preliminary interrogation and to submit a report to the court for a coroner's examination. Wang Chunshun lived at No. 198 Manzhou Road. When he fell, his left eye was bleeding, his right cheek was bruised, and his left leg was injured, suggesting blows from fists. The suspected murderer, Liu Pinglin, was of similar age and also worked as a barber. The cart's registration number was City 3066, and it was carrying wooden boards weighing approximately 800 catties.

An unidentified male corpse was discovered hanging from a tree behind the Chizhi College on Jiangwan Road yesterday morning. The deceased was approximately thirty years old, wearing a grey cloth long gown, a white short shirt, black cloth trousers, and black cloth shoes. Aside from a fan that had fallen on the ground, there were no other belongings. Assassination of Inspector at Cotton Mill 124

Two Individuals Detained in Connection

Zhao Xilin, a native of Bi County who worked as an inspector at the Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill and the Zhonghua No. 1 Knitting Factory on Longjiang Road in Yangshupu, was shot in the kidney and leg by an enemy at 6:40 AM on the 20th of this month in front of the Shenxin factory gate. He was sent to the hospital for treatment. Stray bullets injured Li Litang, the owner of a pancake shop, and Zhang Wenjin, a crab seller from Shaoxing, who died from their injuries. Tao Ruisheng, Xu Sihai, Xu Axian, and three others were also injured. These details have been reported in this newspaper. The day before yesterday afternoon, Zhao Xilin's wife, Wang, learned that Qian Afu, a native of Wuxi residing at No. 3112 Yangshupu Road, was involved in the case. She reported this to the Yangshupu Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Detective Pang Ruiqing to secretly arrest Qian. Another Wuxi native, Qiang Ruxing, was subsequently apprehended at No. 1865 on the same road and taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Station lawyer Li Zhishan presented the case, stating that the two defendants were suspects and requesting interrogation. Zhao Wang also claimed that although the two defendants were not present at the scene, they knew the fugitive murderer. Under questioning, Qian Afu stated that he encountered a friend surnamed "Mou" on the No. 8 tram yesterday, who mentioned that the Zhao Xilin incident was committed by Xiao Changzhou. He added that Xiao Changzhou was his brother from the same mother, and he was shocked to hear about it but did not know the underlying cause of the conflict. He requested clarification. Qiang Ruxing claimed that his friend Tao Rongrong asked him to borrow twenty yuan in foreign currency to help Xiao Changzhou with travel expenses so he could flee elsewhere. He stated that he had nothing to do with the Zhao Xilin incident. Judge Xiao Xiefen reviewed the statements and ordered that they be remanded in custody for further investigation and interrogation at a later date.

One Bandit Commits Two Abduction Cases 125

Xu Zhou, a woman from Taixing residing at No. 3 Pingliang Road, had a daughter named Zhiying, only ten years old, who suddenly disappeared around 4:00 PM on the 15th of this month while playing in front of her house. She was abducted by someone. Despite entrusting others to search for her, she remained untraceable. The day before yesterday at noon, her second landlord, Qi Ganru, who sold tickets on the French Concession tram, was informed that a young girl had been abducted and was being peddled by a bandit at Wu's pancake shop at No. 110 Maidie'an Road. Upon learning this, Qi returned home and told his tenant, Xu Zhou, who then reported it to the Yangshupu Police Station. Detective Zhao Bingyue, along with Dai Jingen and Ge Yongzhen, disguised themselves as customers and went to Wu's pancake shop in the French Concession to investigate. They pretended to buy the girl, negotiated a price of forty yuan with the bandit, Xu Dishan from Jiangbei, and arrested him. They also rescued the child Zhiying and brought them back to the police station. Under interrogation, Xu confessed that he had also abducted his wife's younger sister, Li Xiuying, in his hometown on May 19th of this year. Using the pretext of introducing her to factory work, he brought her to Shanghai and sold her to Tao Laifeng, a resident of Xiaoqiaotou in the Sixteenth Ward, for sixty yuan to be his wife. Detective Zhao Hua also went to the address and brought Li Xiuying back to the police station. The police chief ordered that both girls be temporarily sent to the Women's Shelter and that Xu be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Station representative and lawyer Li Zhishan stated that the defendant had confessed to both cases at the police station and requested strict punishment. Detective Zhao, along with witnesses Dai Jingen, Ge Yongzhen, and the girl's mother, Xu Zhou, also presented their accounts of the incident. Li Xiuying stated that she was originally from the Li Family Village in Jiasi Temple, Taixing, and had been betrothed to Shen Longzi in Caozhenpu, three miles from her mother's home, and had already entered his household as a fostered daughter-in-law. In April of this year, she happened to be returning to her mother's home when she met the defendant, who was her brother-in-law. He tricked her into coming to Shanghai, claiming to recommend her for work in a factory, but she was sold to the Tao family in the Sixteenth Ward to be his wife for sixty yuan. She stated that she now wished to return to her hometown. Under questioning, the defendant admitted to both abduction cases without hesitation. Judge Xiao Xiefen sentenced Xu Dishan to three years of imprisonment as a warning. The girl Xu Zhiying was released to her mother, Xu Zhou. Li Xiuying was temporarily sent to the Women and Children's Relief Association for shelter, and a letter was sent to Taixing County, instructing her family to come to Shanghai to claim her.

Cui Heshang, Destitute and Starving, Attempts Suicide in Huangpu River, A Pathetic Case 126

At eight o'clock the night before last, a man in ragged condition hailed sampan number 1204 at the Hankou Road Customs Wharf, stating that he wanted to cross to the Lan Nidu Wharf in Pudong. When the boat reached the British warship buoy in the outer Huangpu River, the man suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Sampan operator Chu Weilin bravely rescued him in the dark and took him to the Customs Water Police Station. Under interrogation, the man stated that his name was Cui Heshang, forty-one years old, from Hubei Province, and that he had been a pig's bristle merchant. In recent years, his luck had turned bad, his business had failed, and his financial situation had become increasingly dire. He was destitute and starving and would soon die, so he planned to die in Shanghai. He said he only had one friend, residing in Yipin Lane, Baoshan Road, Zhabei. The police chief dispatched Detective Ge Chang to locate his friend so that Cui could be taken away and provided with relief.

Romantic Woman Commits Suicide by Opium 127

The Zhu family, who are originally from Wuxi, live in the Lu Gaojian Meat Shop in the Ji畝地 district of the city. Zhu works to make a living. Recently, Zhu's husband's younger sister, Zhu Xiaomei, nineteen years old, came to Shanghai to stay with her sister-in-law. Unexpectedly, Xiaomei was of a romantic nature and did not return home for several nights. It was obviously improper for a young woman to spend the night outside, so her sister-in-law reprimanded her. Xiaomei felt greatly ashamed and, the day before yesterday, swallowed opium and committed suicide. Upon discovering this, she was immediately taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, but she died. The First Office of the Second District instructed Jiang Pingyang, the local leader, and the Local Court to report the incident. Prosecutor Zhao and others arrived on the scene to investigate. The family collected the body for burial.

The Little Sister-in-Law Elopes with her Brother-in-Law 130

Fang Xuebao is extremely angry and accuses Jin Baifu of denying the elopement.

Fang Xuebao, 31 years old, from Nanjing, lives at No. 23 Wangjiazhai, Hujun Camp, Nanshi, and sells vegetables for a living. His wife, Zhou, 23 years old, from Suzhou, has a bad relationship with her husband, so quarrels are often heard. In May of this year, she suddenly ran away from her husband without a word and disappeared. Fang followed his wife and asked people everywhere, but there was no news. Then he found out that Zhou had been seduced by her brother-in-law, Jin Fubai, and was hiding in Jin's house in Suzhou. Fang followed and met her, but Zhou swore that she would not return to his house. Fang could not do anything and had to return to Shanghai. The day before yesterday, Zhou and Jin Fubai came to Shanghai and returned home. She said to her husband, "Now I regret what I did. I want to grow old with you." Fang was so happy to hear this that he forgot about the past and treated Jin as an honored guest because of their family relationship, and kept him for dinner. Afterwards, Fang went out, and when he returned at about 8 p.m., he suddenly saw that his wife Zhou and his brother-in-law Jin Fubai had packed the clothes and ornaments in the room into parcels. They were in a panic, planning to pack up and run away for the second time. Fang was very suspicious when he saw this, and realized that Zhou's regrets were all lies, and that she had come here to take the property. He was immediately angry and seized the two men and handed them over to Liu Chuanxi, the guard at the 23rd post, and brought them to the first branch of the first district. During the preliminary trial by the director, Fang filed a case and stated the situation, and asked for a strict investigation. Jin Baifu claimed that Fang Zhou was his sister-in-law. Because her husband, Fang Xuebao, was violent and Zhou was beaten if she disobeyed him, she returned to her mother's home in her hometown in May of this year because she was mistreated and did not want to live with Fang Xuebao. Fortunately, her mother repeatedly comforted her, and she changed her mind. So her mother asked me to accompany her to Shanghai today to send her back to Fang's house. Unexpectedly, Fang bit the hand that fed him, and did not appreciate his good intentions, but instead made up lies and accused him. He asked for investigation. Fang Zhou's statement was the same as Jin's. Since the two sides held conflicting statements, they were ordered to prepare a document and submit it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Shanghai Bank Publishes Commodity Survey Series 131

The Survey Department of Shanghai Bank, in order to facilitate understanding of the Shanghai market by all sectors, has specially edited the Shanghai Commodity Survey Series. Page 16

蕢延芳 Does Not Want Empty Talk, Rejects Five-Year Boycott Plan 134

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association previously resolved to have 蕢延芳,徐永祚, and 李權時 draft a five-year plan to boycott Japanese goods, with the goal of maintaining the enthusiasm permanently, to avoid the criticism of a "five-minute" boycott. However, 蕢 and the others considered this matter to be of great importance, beyond the ability of a few individuals. If it was just empty talk on paper without practical benefit, they felt it was unnecessary. Therefore, they submitted a report to the association yesterday, stating: "Regarding the report, your esteemed association has entrusted 延芳,永祚, and 權時 with the task of drafting a five-year plan to boycott Japanese goods. We dare not fail to exert our meager efforts and contribute our humble opinions. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be accomplished by a few people closing their doors and building a car. Furthermore, if it is called a five-year plan to boycott Japanese goods, it should actually be a five-year industrial plan, or a self-sufficiency plan for necessities such as clothing, food, housing, and transportation, which should be achieved through the collective wisdom and efforts of the people of the entire country. Not only are we three, with our limited knowledge, insufficient to shoulder this heavy responsibility, but even the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and people from all walks of life, who are rich in talent, may not be able to undertake this heavy responsibility alone. Moreover, for the success of any industrial plan, it is necessary to consider the country's productivity. Productivity does not only refer to the four tangible elements of land, capital, labor, and enterprise, but also includes intangible factors such as clear politics, social stability, labor-capital cooperation, convenient transportation, and the people's good intentions. We are now motivated by righteous indignation to launch the eighth boycott of Japanese goods, and we intend to take a further step to find a fundamental solution, which is to strive to manufacture domestic goods and plan for a five-year or ten-year industrial plan, which is a great undertaking. However, we should ask whether the four elements of production in our country are currently complete. Even if the four elements of production are complete, or can be made complete, what about the various preconditions for production? Therefore, if we only want to engage in empty talk about a five-year plan to boycott Japanese goods, or an industrial plan, that is all well and good. If we do not want to engage in empty talk, but want to implement the plan, then the problem may not be solved by planning and technology, and the key seems to lie in clear politics, social stability, labor-capital cooperation, transportation recovery, and the people's good intentions. If we can earnestly do these things, then national shame will be erased and the hatred of foreign goods will be eliminated. As for a detailed five-year plan or industrial plan, 延芳 and the others not only do not dare to rashly draft this major plan, but also feel that even if they do draft it, it would only amount to empty talk. This is because the current social and political situation cannot be improved in a day, and therefore is not suitable for any industrial plan or economic self-sufficiency plan. We hereby submit this report for your kind consideration."

Shanghai's Commercial Market Depressed 135

Affected by the Boycott and Flooding, the Quantity of Imports and Exports Has Been Greatly Reduced

The 大美晚報 reported that due to the recent boycott of Japanese goods and the Yangtze River floods, the quantity of commercial goods imported and exported from Shanghai in July and the first half of August has been greatly reduced. Apart from a few batches of textiles and food products shipped to Dalian, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Yingkou, there were very few goods going to other northern ports. To southern ports, only limited quantities of textiles and food products were shipped to Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou. The items shipped from the above ports to Shanghai were sugar, seafood, and a limited amount of white rice. Since the interior suffered from flooding, the shipment of goods to Europe has almost completely stopped. Due to the poor silkworm cocoon harvest this year, the quantity of raw silk shipped to the United States has also been greatly reduced. Tung oil produced in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River cannot be shipped out due to the flood. Imports from Japan have been greatly reduced due to the boycott of Japanese goods. The shipment of goods to Japan has also been temporarily stopped. The goods shipped to the Yangtze River are almost entirely food supplies for disaster relief.

Further News of Intercepted Military Equipment 136

Expected to Be Purchased Entirely by the National Government

The 大陸報 reported that the large quantity of machine guns, rifles, aircraft bullets, and explosives brought by the German ship on Saturday night has now been unloaded and stored in the Lan Road warehouse. When the ship entered Chinese territorial waters, it was heavily armed and escorted along the way by customs patrol boats and more than twenty water police officers until the unloading was completed. This was because the military equipment was originally intended to be shipped to Guangdong, and there were concerns that someone from Guangdong might take the opportunity to hijack the ship, re-export it, and transfer it to a ship bound for Guangdong. According to what was heard last night, the explosives were originally intended for Japan, while the rest of the military equipment was originally intended for Guangdong. The quantity is not yet known with certainty, and the future disposition is still undecided. It is expected that the entire quantity will be purchased by the National Government.

Reaction to the British Public Bus Company's Dismissal of All Ticket Collectors 139

Workers' Assembly Dispersed by Police Yesterday

Declaration Issued, Drivers to Serve as Mediators

Following the strike by all ticket collectors of the British Public Bus Company, the company yesterday continued to operate routes 1, 2, 5, and 9 with difficulty and announced the dismissal of all ticket collectors, hiring new workers. The workers' assembly failed to convene due to police intervention. Yesterday, the drivers offered to mediate, and the workers issued a declaration seeking assistance. The details of yesterday's events are recorded below:

勉强行駛 With Difficulty, Continuing Operation: Starting yesterday, the company continued to send ticket inspectors to replace ticket collectors, barely managing to operate ten buses on route 1 from Jing'an Temple to the Gongyuan Shooting Range, six buses on route 2 from Eryang Bridge to the Gongyuan Shooting Range, three buses on route 5 from Sanmaoge Bridge to the North Railway Station, nine buses on route 9 from Jing'an Temple to the Electric Light Factory, one 'A' special express bus, and one 'C' special express bus, totaling thirty buses. All other routes remain suspended.

工人大會 Workers' Assembly: The Public Bus Strike Committee held a general meeting at 9:00 AM yesterday inside the China Park on Suzhou Road to discuss how to deal with the company's rejection of the nine proposed conditions. It was reported that over 180 ticket collectors and driver representatives were in the middle of discussions when armed detectives from the Lao Zha Police Station arrived and dispersed the meeting. The meeting was thus unable to be completed and was rescheduled. However, all the workers were extremely agitated by the police interference with their assembly.

全體革退 Dismissal of All: According to the British Public Bus Company yesterday, the nine conditions proposed by the ticket collectors had been completely rejected. It was also stated that all 222 striking ticket collectors had been dismissed and 40 new ticket collectors were being trained at the Connaught Road headquarters. Once training is complete, they will be assigned to various routes.

公司損失 Company Losses: Following the strike by all ticket collectors of the Public Bus Company on the 20th, the company has tried to maintain traffic by sending ticket inspectors to perform the duties of the ticket collectors, barely managing to operate a few routes. However, the company's daily business losses are estimated to be over 3,000 yuan. The workers' intangible losses are also countless.

司機會議 Drivers' Meeting: Over 250 drivers of the Public Bus Company, in order to support the ticket collectors, held a representative meeting at 8:00 AM yesterday. The meeting resolved on the spot to first offer mediation and then to join the strike. Yesterday afternoon, three representatives were sent to negotiate with the company. The results are not yet known, and further reports will follow.

工方宣言 Workers' Declaration: The declaration by all striking workers of the British Public Bus Company reads: To the citizens of Shanghai, fellow workers in all factories, we, the public bus workers, are now on strike, causing much inconvenience to you all. We are extremely sorry for this. However, we have had to adopt such a decisive measure due to our own compelling reasons: 1. The global economic panic has further bankrupted China's economy and worsened our lives. The value of gold is high, the value of silver is low, and the prices of all goods are soaring. Although our wages remain the same in nominal terms, they have actually decreased. 2. The company recently switched to using diesel fuel, increasing profits several times over. However, operating diesel engines requires even greater effort. This can be said to be an extension of our working hours. 3. The wages of ticket sellers are low and are not enough to cover monthly expenses. Inevitably, there are occasional instances of taking small advantages. We ourselves find this behavior difficult to condone. If wages were slightly higher, we would definitely not resort to such measures. Originally, our wages were only 20 yuan. After deducting all sorts of unreasonable penalties, such as a fine of one yuan for not jumping off at the next stop, a fine of five jiao for forgetting to close the window, a fine of one yuan for sitting on the bus, a fine of one yuan for not wearing a numbered hat, etc., the actual wages received each month are only a little over ten yuan, which is simply not enough to support one person's life. If there are several people in the family, one can only sit and wait for death. Now the company has added plainclothes ticket inspectors who secretly monitor on the bus. Whenever a ticket seller makes a mistake in punching or sorting tickets, or has a slight dispute with a customer, they are mistakenly accused of taking small advantages. One report is enough to have business suspended. In recent days, more than ten people have been dismissed without any evidence. Citizens of Shanghai, fellow workers in all factories, we are in such cruel treatment conditions that we cannot wait any longer. Because we do not want to starve to death, do not want to see our families separated, and do not want to become slaves, we have unanimously gone on strike to make our demands to the capitalists. We vow not to return to work until our goals are achieved. This is not us disregarding public convenience, this is not us making unreasonable threats. The capitalists are cruel, and we are really forced to this situation. Citizens of Shanghai, fellow workers in all factories, in the process of our struggle with the capitalists, the capitalists will of course use various methods to sabotage us, block us, and spread rumors to slander us. Therefore, all our workers earnestly request that you maintain a fair attitude, stand on the side of our class, and give us practical and powerful assistance in terms of spirit and material. If so, all the workers of the British Public Bus Company will be fortunate, and all the workers of Shanghai will be fortunate.

Please Release Anhui Rice for Transport to Shanghai 141

Letter from Anhui Rice Merchants in Shanghai to the Xiashi Grain Industry Association

Due to Anhui rice being banned from leaving Xiashi by the Public Security Bureau, the Anhui Rice Merchants Association in Shanghai sent a special letter to the Xiashi Grain Industry Association yesterday. The original letter is recorded as follows: Respectfully, we are writing to you because our member Mei Fuqing and others reported to our association that in April of this year, they transported over 2,000 shi of rice from Sanhe to Xiashi, but it remained in storage due to the sluggish market. Recently, the market in Xiashi remains stagnant, and after months of various expenses, the losses have been too great. In the blink of an eye, the time for the new harvest is approaching, and it cannot be delayed any longer. Therefore, we planned to transport it to Shanghai for sale. Unexpectedly, when setting sail, the Public Security Bureau of your town, citing the provincial order banning rice from leaving the province, and also referring to your association's letter of inquiry, etc., prevented it from doing so. Upon investigation, the provincial order banning rice from leaving the province only applies to special Zhejiang rice. There is absolutely no need to prohibit the earlier stored Anhui rice. Now it is being transported to Jiangsu Province, so why is it not allowed to be transported freely? Although the polder fields in Anhui Province suffered from floods this year, there should be mountainous areas that can be harvested. In the future, when new rice is transported to Jiangsu and Zhejiang, many Anhui merchants will likely regard your town as a dangerous place due to such actions, which may have an impact on the people's food supply in the future. Your association is a leader in the rice industry, regulating the people's food supply and showing compassion for merchants' difficulties, which should be taken into consideration. Moreover, the 20th and 21st reports in your town listed the daily market prices, showing that there are more than 100,000 shi of Anhui rice stored, while Zhejiang Province has had a bumper harvest this year. Why worry about a food shortage? Recently, Wenzhou xian rice from Zhejiang Province has been transported to Shanghai for sale, which is puzzling. Based on this, and for the sake of the current difficulties of the merchants and the future food supply of the people, we dare to write to your association, requesting you to quickly consult the Xiashi Public Security Bureau and order the release of the Anhui rice transported to Shanghai by Mei Fuqing and others in order to facilitate circulation and stabilize commerce. We eagerly await your response. Respectfully presented, hoping for a speedy reply.

Recent News from the Local Autonomy Training Institute 149

Continued Enrollment of New Students, Regardless of Gender

The Institute's Address Expands and Relocates to the Southern City

The Local Autonomy Training Institute in this city is currently continuing to run the second phase. Mayor Zhang deeply believes that the purpose of the city government in establishing this institute is to train personnel to handle local autonomy. During the period of political tutelage, the government will appoint people to assist the people in preparing for and implementing autonomy in order to promote constitutional government. The responsibilities are heavy, so the institute is expanding its funding, hiring specialized professors, and raising the level of the students. The original address of the institute on Zhabei Zhiyi Road is now insufficient and the transportation is inconvenient, so a large building at 81 Xieqiao Manufacturing Bureau Road in the southern city has been rented and will be moved there at the beginning of next month.

City Chamber of Commerce Protests Forced Payment of Water Meter Deposits 150

Sent a Letter to the Taxpayer Association for Handling

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayer Association yesterday, stating that on the 12th of this month, it received a letter from the Ironware Industry Association, stating that the factory of Jiang Jinchang, a member of the association, had been using tap water for 13 years since the seventh year of the Republic, and had never delayed payment of water bills. Recently, the tap water company suddenly demanded a deposit of 150 yuan, and threatened to cut off the water supply if payment was not made. The association requested that the Chinese consultant negotiate with the tap water company. It was found that the tap water fees in the concession were directly collected by the tap water company from the landlords. The method was to install branch pipes from the main pipe at the alley entrance to supply water to each household. There were no water meters or deposits. However, when Jiang Jinchang's factory was built in the seventh year of the Republic, Zhoujiazui Road was far from the main water pipe, so a 4-point water pipe was installed separately. At that time, a installation fee of 67 taels of silver was paid. Since the installation, the water bills have never been in arrears. The deposit was originally a guarantee. The factory owner already owns the property and would not damage their reputation for a small amount of water bill. The factory believes that since a deposit of three months' water bill has been collected, monthly fees should not be charged, or interest on the deposit should be set and paid with the user's consent before payment is made. Later, our association sent people to seek your opinion, and you also stated that the factory is an old user of more than ten years, and cannot be compared to a new user installing water pipes whose credit is unknown to the company. The so-called cutting off the water supply and taking strict measures is not the proper way to treat the company's customers. Moreover, there are many users in the concession who have water meters but have not paid deposits, so why should there be such an unreasonable measure for users who have never been in arrears? Furthermore, the tap water expert hired by the company will arrive in Shanghai soon, and all issues can be temporarily put on hold. After deliberation at the 59th Standing Committee meeting of our association, based on the above situation, we have written to the Taxpayer Association to handle the matter accordingly.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was as follows: The weather on the coast here is cloudy with strong northeasterly gusts and intermittent rain. The weather is extremely bad over the East China Sea and along the coast from the mouth of the Yangtze River to Fuzhou, with a violent cyclone/hurricane continuing to move northwestward, approaching the coast between Wenzhou and Taizhou. There are strong northeasterly winds on the Yellow Sea. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 90.1 degrees and the lowest was 79.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 96.1 degrees and the lowest was 72.3 degrees.

Letters Received

Respectfully, I read in your newspaper's local news column that the family of Zhao Shixi, a resident of Dongchijiabang in Hongzhen, North Shanghai, was targeted by bandits. At 11:00 PM the night before, three bandits suddenly came and robbed 21 silver dollars. Zhao was shot by the bandits, fell to the ground injured, and was barely breathing. His family reported the incident to the Fourth Office of the Fifth District. I was very surprised. Upon investigation, our office has not received any report from the people about the above incident, and the area is not under the jurisdiction of our office. It seems that there was a mistake in the investigation. I am writing this letter to request you to investigate and correct the information. With best wishes, this is addressed to the editor of the Shenbao, from the Fourth Office of the Fifth District of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, August 24.

Respectfully, your newspaper reported on the 23rd on the case of impersonating officials to order military goods. The defendant, Bi Ke, claimed, "I have a lot to say, but all the important documents are with my lawyer, Pyleme. Now Pyleme is not appearing in court today because I am unable to pay the legal fees, and the documents have not been returned. This situation is very detrimental to the ethics of lawyers." I was very surprised to read this. Upon investigation, this lawyer received a letter written in Bi Ke's own hand on the 21st of this month, stating that when the court was scheduled to hear the case at 9:00 AM on the 22nd, please don't go to the court at that time. The letter can prove that what was written in your newspaper, that I was unable to pay the legal fees, is also incorrect. When Bi Ke hired this lawyer to handle the case, the legal fees had already been paid. This lawyer's non-appearance on the 22nd was to follow the instructions of the client. What was written in your newspaper must have been a mistake in reporting. I am writing to request correction. This is to send you peace. Lawyer Pyleme, August 24, 20th year.

Free Talk

World Small Things 156

— Sea Passenger

Invisible Glasses

All people with nearsightedness or farsightedness in both eyes have to wear glasses on their noses to aid their vision. However, most fashionable men and women generally do not think glasses are a fashionable accessory and are often unwilling to wear them. The degree of nearsightedness and farsightedness will inevitably increase as a result. Now, the British have invented a new type of invisible glasses that can solve this difficult problem. The inventor is an employee of a large eyeglasses company. He made a very small lens, slightly like a disc, which is tightly embedded between the upper and lower eyelids, covering the eyeball, so that people cannot see that he is wearing glasses from a few feet away. Because the lens is exceptionally thin, it is like nothing.

These glasses are most suitable for actors. Usually, those who suffer from nearsightedness and wear glasses cannot wear glasses in the play they are playing. Even if he is good at performing, he has to hire someone else. As soon as these invisible glasses come out, any character can be played without any difficulty.

Mr. Feng is Immortal 157

— Sun Choucheng

Mr. Feng Junmu of Cixi, with his extensive knowledge and noble integrity, is a great master of Confucianism. His doorstep is always full of people seeking to learn characters from him. His "Returning Wind" collection is known throughout the country. In his later years, he lived in Shanghai, and he associated with many famous people of his time. People like Zhu Guwei, Xiao Song, Cheng Zida, and Wu Changshuo all admired his writing and respected his actions. Their carriages often visited each other, and they were as happy as old friends. Moreover, both Xiao Song and Wu Changshuo had last words, insisting that Mr. Feng inscribe their tombs. This shows how his writing and morality were admired by the world. He passed away in Shanghai on May 18 of this year, after suffering from illness for several months from winter to summer. Friends and associates visited him, their feet wearing a path to his courtyard. Some stayed up all night to serve him, unwilling to leave. When he passed away, they all burst into tears, unable to control their grief. The memorial service was attended by hundreds of people. If he had not possessed great virtue and cultivated himself internally, how could he have moved his peers to such an extent? On the 23rd of the month, Zhu Guwei, Wang Yiting, Chen Qihui, and Zhang Yongni launched a public memorial service. His disciples, Chen Bulei, Wu Jingxiong, and others, wore black gauze armbands as a sign of mourning and attended the meeting. There were more than a hundred people in attendance. Chen Qihui was chosen to preside over the memorial service because he had the deepest relationship with Mr. Feng. He was asked to report on Mr. Feng's brief history. Chen said that he and Mr. Feng had been friends since childhood. He knew that Mr. Feng's writing was already brilliant when he returned to Cixi from Songjiang at the age of fourteen. Mr. Feng was born with a good appearance, was intelligent and pure, and could recognize all the classics and hundreds of schools of thought at first sight, as if he had been blessed by heaven. At that time, his predecessors all regarded him as a child prodigy. Everyone knew that Mr. Feng was kind and approachable and did not compete with the world. They did not know that his views were also very radical when he was young. After drinking, he would write articles that were arrogant and disregardful of everything. Later, because he was teaching in Hangzhou, he was noticed by the authorities. His family was afraid that he would cause trouble, so they said that his mother was ill and sent a telegram to call him back home. He was naturally filial and, after receiving the telegram, regardless of whether the tide of the Cao'e River was favorable or not, he rushed home at the risk of his life, arriving home within twenty-four hours. He made friends regardless of poverty or wealth and did not change his principles due to life or death. However, when it came to discussing writing, he was unwilling to show weakness even to his closest friends. He was very frugal in his own life, but he did his best to help his poor relatives. He was good at guiding and educating young learners. He would always praise even the smallest abilities. First, he would arouse their interest, and then he would encourage them to improve their skills. Therefore, his disciples respected and loved him as they would their fathers and brothers. Wu Jingxiong's eulogy read: "For decades, he has been a mentor, with ten thousand volumes in his chest. I, as a young man, once benefited from his teachings." "Just one year away from his sixtieth birthday, his spirit entered my dreams. I cannot bear to read his will, 'Returning Wind.'" As a result, because Mr. Feng's posthumous works included several volumes of essays from the Returning Wind Hall, several volumes of poems, one volume of ci poems, several volumes of notes, and several volumes of miscellaneous works, none of which have been published, it would be a great pity to let them be lost. Therefore, eight old friends, including Chen Qihui, and disciple representatives, including Chen Bulei and Sha Menghai, were elected to preside over the printing of Mr. Feng's collected poems and essays. The disciples also formed the Returning Wind Society, which will hold meetings and offer sacrifices on Mr. Feng's death anniversary every year in order to connect the feelings of fellow students and commemorate Mr. Feng's great virtue.

Yang Xuejiu's Poems 158

Visiting Yan Ziling's Fishing Platform

Not seeking wealth or avoiding ennoblement.

Alone I fish amidst flowing waters and towering mountains.

Alas, Yan Gong is now gone.

Only a clear sorrow remains on the solitary hill.

Passing the Songjun Villa

Emerald green on the opposite west tower.

Outside the gate, a spring flows over the stones.

Such serenity is truly extraordinary.

Floating clouds and wealth are not needed.

Mountain Village Rain Scene

Bamboo fence and thatched cottage slant in the rain.

Mountain colors are hazy, veiled by a thin mist.

Willows droop along the path, all in tears.

Where solitary smoke rises, there is a home.

The above three seven-character quatrains were written by Xuejiu during his spring tour of the Fuchun River. They have been on my desk for a long time and are about to be thrown into the servant's word basket. I love their clarity and Song-like style. I quickly presented them to Mr. Shoujuan for publication in the Free Talk. Yang Xue also attached this note.

My Views on Grain Storage 159

— Tianxu I Sheng

Recently, I have been suffering from hemorrhoids, making it painful to walk, sit, or lie down, so I have not been attending social gatherings for a long time. Yesterday, while in bed due to illness, I read in the newspaper a list of donors for grain storage, and I saw the name Chen Yiyuan. I don't know if there is another person with that name, or if it is a mistake for the character "Xu". I have a humble opinion that I would like to contribute to the authorities in the hope that it will be adopted. I have always thought that the most important element of the grain storage system should be replacing the old with the new, taking from the surplus and supplementing the insufficient, so that everyone will be willing to participate and not just watch. It would be best to establish a method where every donation of ten yuan to the grain storage fund would entitle the donor to withdraw one dan of rice each month, based on the prevailing rice price, with a maximum limit in yuan. The price should only be allowed to fall, not rise. For those who store for half a year or a year, the price should be reduced by five percent each month according to the market price, and storage receipts should be given, with rice issued according to the predetermined monthly period. Delivery costs would be calculated separately. For example, if one stores rice for a year, paying 120 yuan, it would be issued in twelve monthly installments. The price for the second month would be reduced by one jiao, and the price for the twelfth month would be reduced by six jiao. If this were done, everyone would be happy to have the security of a bargain. Businesses, factories, schools, organizations, and households of all sizes would enthusiastically invest to prevent the impact of high rice prices. If a family of one hundred were to store sixteen dan of rice per month, they would collect a fund of 160 yuan. With a population of three million in Shanghai, storing about 160,000 dan of rice per month, and with the purchase price at thirteen yuan, it would amount to about two million yuan. When starting to raise funds for grain storage, cash of 1.6 million yuan would be received successively. The money would be deposited in the treasury to earn interest, and rice would be paid out each month as needed. This would require purchasing 60,000 dan of rice each day, costing only 800,000 yuan. Selling 50,000 dan of rice, with a supplemental price of three yuan, would yield a daily supplemental cash income of 150,000 yuan. The actual amount of money needed would only be 200,000 yuan, and even this amount may not be necessary. After all, there must be a surplus in the turnover of funds. Everyone is worried about future difficulties and will not just think about the present. Therefore, many will choose to store for a year or half a year. If we assume that the average storage period is four months, we would collect 6.4 million yuan in storage funds, and with good credit, raising ten million would not be difficult. If we adopt this strategy, starting with me, storing for half a year would amount to nearly a thousand. It would also be easier to solicit donations. Otherwise, asking someone to donate is tantamount to receiving a favor, and the obligation to reciprocate is endless. In the past ten years, I have felt this difficulty and have regarded it as a debt, even worse than a debt. I believe others must feel the same way. Therefore, I offer this humble opinion as a way to capitalize on the situation, as described above. I hope it will be adopted. (No reward is necessary.)

North Railway Station Anecdotes 160

— Aicheng

The sensational Zhujing infanticide case involving Wang Tao and Xia Aqing has already resulted in the Jinshan County government sentencing them to death and twelve years imprisonment respectively. This matter could have been considered closed, but Wang Tao refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Suzhou High Court. The Jinshan County government specially transferred the entire case file and the three major criminals to Shanghai from Jin, traveling on the 25th Shanghai-Changzhou commuter train on the afternoon of the 19th. By about 2:00 PM, the three criminals had boarded the train. Station personnel were competing to read the latest infanticide reports. I also went with a friend to observe. By this time, the train was already packed. Wang Tao and the other two were bound with hemp rope. Xia Aqing even had iron shackles on her feet. Wang Tao's face was round and large, and her hair was neatly styled. She was dressed in skirts and looked down, as if overcome with shame. The wet nurse sat next to Wang Tao, constantly fanning her mistress to relieve the heat. Xia Aqing was feigning sleep. In addition to the three criminals, the Jinshan County government also sent bailiffs to escort them. The onlookers were discussing the case, some criticizing her as an adulteress, others condemning her son's absurdity. The three criminals remained silent. Their sorrow was evident.

This time, Chairman Chiang came to Shanghai from Jiangxi to act as a pallbearer for Madame Soong. Because the Communists had not been eliminated, he returned to Nanjing early on the morning of the 20th. At 9:00 AM, the area around the North Railway Station was already closed to traffic. Military police were heavily deployed, and secret agents were everywhere. Soldiers were drawing their guns as if ready to fire. More than a hundred armed police officers stood on the platform. Soon, more than ten members of a military band arrived. Everyone was eager to catch a glimpse of the Chairman's imposing presence and waited with bated breath. At 9:30 AM, the train slowly moved, but the Chairman was still nowhere to be seen. Then an officer arrived, panting, and said that the Chairman had already left and the lockdown could be lifted. It was hard to tell what was true. No one knew when he had boarded the train. Some said that the Chairman did not like being seen off and boarded the train at Zhenru. However, it caused the military police to rush around for half a day, which was also quite a hardship.

There are many scams at the North Railway Station, but there are also those who are wandering outside due to poverty. A few days ago, a woman and a young child pleaded with the ticket seller, saying that they were stranded and wanted to return to Suzhou but had no money. They begged for assistance. The ticket clerk, feeling sorry for them, raised over a yuan and bought them a ticket, personally escorting them onto the train. Those who saw it praised him for his righteous and courageous act.

Unchanged Passion After Twenty-Five Years 161

— Jun

In 1906, in the Borja region near Rome, a man named Cesare was sentenced to thirty years imprisonment for the crime of killing a wealthy lawyer named Branzier. At the end of last month, his sentence expired, and he was released from prison. He then married a woman named Lamartine. It is said that this Lamartine was in love with Cesare even before he committed the crime. Because her lover was imprisoned, she remained unmarried. However, up to five years ago, she was still hesitant. But for the past five years, she was confident that her fiancé would eventually be released, and she waited with unwavering determination. Now, she has finally married him and is living a happy life. It can be said that true love conquers all. Counting from the time her fiancé was imprisoned, it has been twenty-five years.

Indian Travel Notes (90) 162

— Linghua

That evening, Reverend Naren Misha invited me to his home and to observe a wedding ceremony of his townspeople, which was somewhat similar to those in China. The groom rides a horse and wears flowers. The drums and music went to the bride's house. The father also went to celebrate. They met and exchanged gifts. When a guest went, he was also given a wreath. Before leaving, the guest was given a coconut. Sometimes a perfume atomizer was used to spray the passing guests. This kind of wedding, where the parents arranged the marriage, was the old style. The new style took place in a public place, like in China. But the new style has not yet become widespread in India.

On the morning of the 12th, I met with C.H. Bose. Bose was a businessman I stayed with before. He told me about a great immortal's place of cultivation, which was located in the high mountains and forests northwest of Nepal. You can get there by going up from Delhi. He was also going to go there to abandon the mortal world. There were many immortals living in that forest, eating fruit and drinking water, and practicing meditation. As for the great immortal, he could stay in the snow without feeling cold. Bose was a wealthy merchant without a wife. He told me many truths and asked me what I would do if I encountered a tiger or a snake. He said that he had encountered a tiger twice and a large snake once. He would only silently recite a prayer. If they ate him, he would save himself a lot of trouble. If they left him alone, he would accept it. He was not afraid. I thought it was strange that Bose had always lived with others, but now he was saying this. But it was a common view among Indians. Gandhi viewed the British bullets with the same attitude. Bose showed me a map and said that east of Nepal was a small independent country that did not belong to Britain or China. It was located west of Bhutan, east of Nepal, and south of Tibet, on the high mountains. The place was called Sikkim.

There were many people there who practiced Taoism and studied Buddhism. He had two places to go. One was the place where the great immortal lived, northwest of Nepal, where the Ganges River originated. The other was east of Nepal, in the Darjeeling area, in Sikkim. I heard that the British did not allow people to enter Tibet without British permission, so investigating it was not easy. I thought that the Himalayas were the highest mountains in the world. Indian culture originated here. Hinduism was the mother of Buddhism, and Hinduism originated from this mountain and the Ganges River. Buddha was influenced by Hinduism, so he also went to the snowy mountains to practice and preached by the Ganges River. I hope that Buddhist disciples from our country will come and visit together, as the snowy mountains are near Tibet, to appreciate its flavor. Bose wanted to invite me to visit the high mountain immortals for a month, but I was unable to due to illness. In short, there are many strange things in the Himalayas. I hope that people from our country will explore them. A certain Japanese man had stayed in India for more than ten years and wrote a travelogue about Tibet, bringing a servant who was Chinese. The servant's wife was Tibetan. The Indians still often mentioned it. Our Chinese people have no lack of capital, but some are focused on increasing their wealth, while others are busy gambling day and night. The secrets of the Himalayas are left to the Japanese to explore. The Chinese do not know about it. The Daoist Jie Shi was determined to go, but had to stop due to economic difficulties, which is a pity.

Random Notes from a Northeast Survey (1) 163

— Liu Suijiu

(1) The Northeast and Manchuria-Mongolia

I have lived in the Northeast for over a year. During this year, in addition to lecturing at Northeast University, I have also traveled to various places from time to time to conduct surveys and interviews, collecting a great deal of research data on various aspects of the Northeast. What I have seen and heard is even more countless.

I often study the word "Northeast" as a substitute for "Manchuria-Mongolia," and I feel that it is not appropriate. Because "Northeast" is a directional and indefinite name, while "Manchuria-Mongolia" is a geographically defined term. If we rashly say "Northeast," the listener will not know what we are referring to, especially when speaking to foreigners. If we mention "Manchuria-Mongolia" to anyone, they will immediately understand that we are referring to China's three eastern provinces and Inner and Outer Mongolia. Therefore, the Japanese use "Manchuria-Mongolia" instead of the word "Northeast," which they have no choice but to do. Some Chinese say that this is because the Japanese intend to divide the Northeast. In fact, if the Japanese or Europeans call it "Northeast," they are clearly referring to the Northeast of their own country or a specific Northeast that they want to refer to, rather than the Northeast within China's territory. Therefore, I use the term "Northeastern China" as the title, which is easier to understand and can be used as an international common name.

What we today call the Northeast was indeed the base of the Manchu and Mongol peoples. There is no denying that Manchuria-Mongolia was originally Jianzhou, owned by the Han people. Mongolia has also benefited from the influence of the Han people. Whether it was still owned by the Han people in prehistoric times is a question for archeology.

(2) Overview of Northeastern University

I have been interested in the problem of Northeastern China for many years. After leaving Wuhan University during the summer vacation last year, I traveled to Dalian and Shenyang. Then I received an invitation from Northeastern University, which gave me more convenience in studying the problem of Northeastern China.

Northeastern University was established in the eleventh year of the Republic of China (1922), thanks to the efforts of Xie Yinchang (from Jiangsu), the director of education in Fengtian Province. He worked hard on the planning and fundraising. At that time, the plan was completed, but the funds were not available. Later, he discussed it with Wang Yongjiang, the governor of the province, and urged him to serve as the president of the university. Wang asked how much money was needed. Xie proposed a budget of two million yuan. Wang smiled and nodded, saying that for the sake of Northeastern education, he was willing to work hard to exchange the position of a university president for two million yuan. The matter was then completed. Xie resigned from his position as director due to overwork and went to Harbin to recuperate. After that, Wang Yongjiang joined forces with the governors of Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces to jointly fund the establishment of a university with science and engineering departments based on the original Shenyang Advanced Normal School, and established liberal arts and law departments based on the public literary vocational school. He also obtained permission from the Qing imperial family to allocate 400 mu of official land in front of Zhaoling Mausoleum, excluding the white pine trees, as the site for the Northeastern University factory. The total capital was 2.8 million yuan. In total, the entire university covered an area of more than 1,580 mu. The liberal arts and law schools and student dormitories cost about one million yuan. There were also science and engineering school buildings, science and engineering student dormitories, education school buildings, and education student dormitories, each costing tens of thousands of yuan. There was also a president's office building.

Yarn Flower and Yarn Market Steady 169

The yarn market remains calm and weak. Due to the overall downturn, poor environment, and falling raw material prices, speculators are selling off, Japanese merchants are selling, and Cantonese merchants are also closing out positions. However, actual sales have been maintained recently, and some Sichuan merchants are relatively bullish. Therefore, there are still many who want to go long, and a major player is still engaging in frequent trading. As for the overseas flower and yarn situation, it is still in a state of despair. The local situation will not escape the predicament of hovering for the time being. Significant changes are expected to occur after the delivery of this month.

People's Standard Slightly Brisk: The People's Standard market opened with a slight increase in extra cotton. There were fewer sellers in the market, but the telegraphs for third-grade yarn indicated a downward trend, with each month increasing by 1.23 cash. Cotton Market Turns from Promising to Withered 170

The cotton market started firm but then fell. American cotton rose slightly by over ten pounds, but Dongyang third-grade cotton fell back. The talk that the United States would ban cotton planting next year, which was mentioned the previous day, is feared to be unlikely to materialize. People's confidence has weakened again. However, most local cotton merchants have a strong desire to go long because of the upcoming holiday season, the importance of the weather, and the fact that prices are already low. Unexpectedly, gold prices fell sharply in the afternoon. Japanese merchants, seeing the worsening situation, sold off one after another. According to Japanese merchant sources, there is talk of a second production of American cotton of about 16 million bales. As a result, the market situation has slightly loosened, but the competition among foreign firms is extremely fierce, and prices are very low. The future situation is difficult to be optimistic about.

Hankou Standard Moves Downstream: The Hankou Standard market opened firm in the morning with strong buying interest. Due to the slight increase in American cotton and concerns about stormy weather, each month rose by two cash. Later, due to unfavorable news, prices fell slightly. As a result, distant months rose by 0.5 to 1 cash, while near months fell by 2 cash. Upon hearing that gold prices had fallen sharply in the afternoon, Japanese merchants sold off, and the market sentiment weakened greatly. Each month fell by 2 to 4 cash. The total transaction volume was 95,300 dan. It was found that the sales included 2,000 dan from Changli, 2,900 dan from Shenji, 2,500 dan from Ruida, 2,100 dan from Tianlong, 2,000 dan from Mingde, 2,800 dan from Gongtai, 2,000 dan from Dafeng, 2,200 dan from Meiji, and 1,500 dan from Xincheng. U.S. Bank Loans to Cotton Farmers 172

A New York dispatch on the 22nd stated that to help cotton farmers suffering from overproduction, the First National Bank of Atlanta, Georgia, is prepared to immediately loan farmers 80% of the market price for four to six months. The total capital of the bank and its branches is over 150 million.

High Prices and Clear Sales of Indian Cotton Last Week 173

The Bombay market was quiet last week, with prices falling slightly by 5 rupees following American cotton. According to exporters and manufacturers, Indian cotton seems more expensive than American cotton, so trading is quite slow. The local market price, since the publication of the all-India cotton field forecast, was particularly firm due to the bullish factors. However, it was soon overturned by unfavorable news from overseas. Spot trading was quiet and uneventful. It is doubtful whether Japanese and European exporters can trade at the current market prices. The following is a summary of last week's statistics (in thousands of bales):

Grain and Rice Prices Slightly Weak 174

Arrivals in the South City yesterday were slightly sluggish, while stocks in the district remained tight. Transactions between urban and rural shops were stagnant again. Due to the stability of the Xin Zha market and the large accumulation of goods, people's confidence was weak, and transactions were not as good as before. Sellers had to soften their stance due to the weakening sales market. Early rice prices fell by another dime, and late rice sales were even more sluggish. Market prices also continued to decline due to abundant supply, with medium-grade rice falling even more sharply. According to the situation of early and late rice, prices have been declining sharply in recent days, and arrivals are becoming scarcer. Although there is not much premium Luxiang pointed rice, only top-grade materials are selected, resulting in a fatigued decline.

The source of goods for various merchants in Xin Zha is still thin, and there is still a large amount of accumulated cargo in the river. In terms of transactions in the city, shops are purchasing inventory of late rice the most due to the light rain. Prices are high for fixed-price goods but weak for other grades. Although the source of thick japonica rice from Suzhou, Changzhou, Yixing, and Jiangyin is small, transactions are quiet, and prices have not risen or fallen. Although there is not much premium Yanglu pointed rice, only the freshest is selected. The market presents a mediocre state. Due to insufficient sources of goods and good sales, the situation in Bianyin Yuan Yuan is slightly weaker. New japonica rice arrivals and sales are evenly matched, and prices remain unchanged.

Foreign Firms Peddling Small-Grain Rice 175

The foreign rice market situation yesterday was still not improving, because various merchants had no need for it, and customers in need were mostly blocked by floods, making transportation impossible. Local digestion is good, but the daily arrival of lower-grade rice from the river is increasing, and prices are also falling, so there is no attention paid to foreign rice. Previously, there was interest in medium-grain rice, but there have been no further inquiries recently. However, foreign firms received telegrams from abroad stating that small-grain rice shipped in September was priced at 6.55 taels. The merchants immediately tried to peddle it in the market, but importers believed that the Shanghai standard price of 13-14 yuan was too expensive and remained on the sidelines, with no transactions. There are also no transactions in spot goods. The total floating inventory in the market is about 30,000 units, while speculators and local buyers have about 100,000 units. There is no floating inventory of guest Xian rice in the market, but speculators and local buyers still hold about 10,000 to 20,000 bags. The other day, 4,200 bags of late Jiangxi machine rice were sold for 13.5 to 13.12 yuan, also within the control of Zhongguan cargo.

Flour Prices Loosen and Fall 176

The market has been stepping back this month.

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month generally showed a loosening and falling trend, with quotations for foreign wheat continuing to fall by about 0.2 to 0.4 yuan. Most people believe that the American wheat famine in China must succeed, given the circumstances. The foreign wheat already ordered by various factories is sufficient to meet current actual sales. With each additional 10% completed, they feel that their chips are getting bigger, so the psychology of most people is gloomy. This month's delivery is imminent, and the transaction volume on the exchange is said to be around 2 million bags, mostly by outsiders, with very few actual sales, resulting in a gradual decline in recent days and a downward trend. Distant months are also being dragged down due to weak buying interest. As a result, this month fell by 1.5 points compared to the previous week, September fell by 1.25 points, October/November fell by 1.5 points, December fell by 1 point, and January fell by 0.75 points.

Wheat Futures Market Weak Near, Firm Distant 177

Yesterday, the wheat futures market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, presented a situation of weakness in the near months and stability in the distant months. The near month is approaching delivery, and many outsiders are gradually selling off, while manufacturers have no intention to buy, so the market inevitably fell. The distant months were relatively stable because inland merchants were either closing out their near-term positions or buying into distant months. As a result, this month was slightly down by 1 point compared to the previous day, September/October were up by 2 points, November was up by 1 point, December was up by 2 points, and January was up by 1 point. The spot wheat market is gradually becoming quiet. Arrivals are not moving, and sales are limited. The whole market opened with Yangzhou wheat at 3.7472 yuan and cooked wheat at 3.82 yuan, totaling 1,200 bags, which were handled by Fuxin Huafeng.

Sugar Market: Raw and White Sugar Trends Firm 178

Taikoo Sugar Turns Strong After Falling

Yesterday, sugar market reports from producing areas indicated that the markets in Cuba, New York, and Java were very quiet with no trading sessions held by market associations. The initial price of Dutch 24-grade raw white sugar was 11.6 taels, but there was a shortage of sellers. The market later rose to 11.65 taels, and the market sentiment was still strong. 20-grade medium white sugar was 11.1 taels, Cuban ocean sugar was 10.01 taels, and bowl blue was 8.7 taels, and the market was stable. Sales of Taikoo sugar were very scarce. Furthermore, with the exchange rate turning higher, people's confidence weakened, and the market turned down. B-mark was 12.05 taels, DY-mark was 11.875 taels, HX-mark was 11.7 taels, AM-mark was 11.45 taels. Buyers were still active, and the market was tight. Taikoo O25 opened yesterday at 9.4 taels per 100 bags. Huaxin sold 200 bags of slightly oily goods at 9.1 taels. The company also offered oily bag number 10 Dutch red at 696 bags for 9.55 yuan. Zhenxiang sold 1,500 bags of number 9 Dutch red at 9.6 taels, and the market was quite firm.

An Overview of the Piece Goods Market 179

The piece goods market has undergone tremendous changes since the boycott. The sluggishness of sales is unprecedented. However, the severe floods in various provinces are also a major reason. In previous years at this time, autumn sales would have begun, and buyers would have flocked in. This year, however, it is as rare as morning stars. Chinese piece goods once saw an increase, but now they are also lifeless. East goods have been suspended for a long time due to strict inspections, and the Yangtze River basin is also stagnant, so the downward trend is quite fierce, with a tendency to plummet. This is because the goods ordered in August have gradually arrived in Shanghai, but actual sales have stopped. Merchants are urging delivery very urgently, so they have to sell them at a loss, resulting in considerable losses. Inventory of West goods is extremely scarce, and even when there are comparable goods, the asking prices are surprisingly high and difficult to sell, so they are also completely immobile. The piece goods industry has always regarded autumn as a major sales period. Given the situation this year, it is feared that it will be difficult to develop in the future. Yesterday, the coarse cloth market also fell sharply, with Jubaopen 9-pound cloth at 4.85 taels, Cat Wufu at 4.5 taels, and Santu Sanlu 11-pound cloth at 5.5 taels. 13-pound cloth was also down by 0.05 yuan. However, Wannianqing fine cloth was quite brisk, with Lixu at 9.45 taels. The price of fine cloth from Japanese factories has fallen by 0.02-0.03 yuan in recent days. The production of fine Chinese serge, gabardine, and tribute cloth has gradually increased, but the sentiment of customers is quite soft, so there is no excitement.
