Book Introduction

Sports Field Guide 198

— Zimei

Written by Wang Zhuangfei…Published by Shanghai Qin Fen Bookstore

The sparseness of our country's sports publications is a vivid reflection of the immaturity of the sports industry, and it is also the reason for the immaturity of the sports industry. Among these sparse sports publications, especially those on social sports, we have rarely seen one. The seeming progress but lack of advancement of social sports is not surprising.

Recently, an "echo in the empty valley" appeared. The "Sports Field Guide" was published by Qin Fen Bookstore at No. 39 Xinmin Village, Malong Road, Shanghai. After reading it, there are indeed many insightful arguments, and the methods are all practical. It is truly a well-intentioned original work, making a significant contribution to our country's social sports.

Wang Zhuangfei, the author of the Sports Field Guide, has more than ten years of experience in managing the Shanghai Public Sports Field. He has been diligently working hard and never making any comments. Therefore, we only know him as a doer, not a theorist. In fact, words and actions are mutually supportive. Those who can do it can also speak it. Perhaps Mr. Wang's silence in the past was because his research had not yet reached a certain stage, and he was unwilling to publish it easily.

In his introduction, the author discusses the reasons for the poor performance of public sports fields in our country, pinpointing two points: (1) Each sports field has too little funding; (2) Most people have no spare time. His conclusion is, "To compensate for these two shortcomings, we must make the majority of people aware of the danger of the decline of social sports and have the desire to work together for construction. Not only the education authorities should do this, but the first and second chapters of this book repeatedly focus on the effectiveness of social sports and the needs of public sports fields, for nothing more than this."

He also has some very sincere words regarding the implementation of social sports: "I am confident that there is no fixed method for managing a public sports field. To be loyal to the task, to strive to increase the number of people exercising, and to complete the effectiveness of sports, how to realize the ideal, how to eliminate obstacles, always pay attention and be constantly mindful. All very practical methods will come spontaneously. Sticking to established methods is not feasible." Therefore, his implementation methods are entirely based on experience and provide a faithful report, as detailed in Chapters 3 to 8, without exaggeration or secrecy, covering all the content.

(1) In terms of theory, enthusiastically call on the majority of people to work hard on the construction of social sports—Chapters 1 and 2.

(2) In terms of methods, faithfully report more than ten years of experience in managing sports fields, for everyone's reference—Chapters 3 to 8.

Chapter 1 is "School Sports and Social Sports." Its main point is to clarify that the importance of social sports is no less than that of school sports, and that school sports must be carried out in conjunction with social sports to be effective. There are several thought-provoking words in it: "...Looking at the overall picture, in terms of merit and practical examination, I dare to say that sports is a necessary education in life, and it is also an education that cannot be lacking for a single day. Humans have differences in gender, age, intelligence, strength, wealth... The need for sports is the same. At most, it is just a change in quantity and method. Because a healthy body, a sharp mind, a happy spirit, useful skills, and a mentality and habits that adapt to the environment, whether you are male or female, young or old, intelligent or foolish, strong or weak, rich or poor... are all urgently needed now or in the future, that is, the statutes and detailed rules of the playground for children, the "Construction and Equipment" chapter, lists the construction equipment that should be available in various sports fields, constantly and continuously seeking. The degree of connection is not much different from the relationship between water and fish, and sunshine and rain to flowers and trees. Therefore, having sports within the school and no sports outside the school is fundamentally untenable. School sports being more important than social sports, and discussing social sports after completing school sports, is also an unreasonable proposition." His conclusion is, "The establishment of public sports fields must not be missing in the entire education plan, especially in China, where emphasis on literature and neglect of martial arts has become a habit."

In my personal opinion, the most valuable part of the entire book is Chapter 3, "Strategies for Managing Public Sports Fields." With a clear vision, the author decisively reveals the strategies for managing sports fields: (1) To get the majority of people to come to the field to exercise; (2) To make the people who come to the field to exercise develop a strong interest; (3) To enable people who enjoy exercising to achieve the most perfect sports effects. I think the facilities of public sports fields and social sports, despite the thousands of ways they can be, cannot escape these three goals. If even one point is mistaken, there is a danger of going astray. Therefore, attracting a few athletes to support the facade is not a good sports field. People come and go, tasting briefly, and that is not a good sports field either. Although the sports field is very lively, it is just blindly doing things without enabling each individual to have a courageous and healthy body, a happy spirit, and a modest attitude, and that is not a good sports field either. In other words, residents near the sports field should all come to the sports field, those who have a fixed time to exercise should come to the sports field every day, and over time, they will all become strong and promising talents, as if cast from a model. At this point, the public sports field will not fail its mission. If sports fields are widely established throughout our country, and each sports field reaches this standard, then social stability, national consolidation, and the rise of the nation will inevitably occur.

Comrades who manage sports fields, do not be discouraged, thinking that the obstacles in front of you are too great to follow the goals and move forward. You must know that for every effort you put in, there is a corresponding effect. With a corresponding effect, there is trust from a segment of the population. With trust from a segment of the population, you will get assistance from part of the population. From near to far, accumulate small amounts to make a large amount. When outsiders trust and the effectiveness is great, all obstacles can be turned into nothing. Therefore, I wholeheartedly agree with the three goals proposed by the author.

The following chapters on "Organization," "Construction and Equipment," "Opening," "Management," and "Work" can be said to be all means to achieve these three goals. Because the author's writing is based on experience everywhere, faithfully reporting, secretly using arguments to alert key points, and the steps are well-organized. What is particularly wonderful is that each chapter lists specific examples to clearly show methods. For example, the "Organization" chapter lists the construction and equipment methods of public sports fields and simple sports equipment, and the architectural equipment methods, all with drawings, clear dimensions. The "Opening" chapter lists the timetable for opening the various sports fields and various parts. The "Management" chapter lists the regulations for entry, field rental, item borrowing, item deposit, bathing, swimming, etc., as well as procedures for field cleaning, equipment inspection, and worker deployment. The "Work" chapter divides the programs into performances, lectures, slogans, publications, equipment, organizing competitions, guiding encouragement... all with very detailed and concrete methods that can teach people to follow the diagram. In these many substantial reports, I am convinced that the author still does not lose his true colors as a practitioner.

I dare not say that the Sports Guide is a perfect and flawless social sports book, but I dare say that it is a pioneer in our country's research on social sports. From this, we can recognize and solve problems such as what a public sports field is, why a public sports field is established, and how a public sports field should be managed.

For such useful books, personnel managing sports administration and students specializing in sports should have a copy in hand. Even those who study education and care about social issues should read it carefully.

Shanghai Market

Theater News 199

Yongyi Film Company declared that the company was founded by the famous martial arts star Zhao Yongni. Ms. Zhao has been engaged in film for more than ten years and has starred in more than 30 films, with extremely rich experience. She recently plans to start filming a martial arts and love epic film "Shanxi Good Fellow." The plot is extremely bizarre and tortuous, magnificent and splendid, creating a new record for national films. Ms. Zhao will personally direct and star in the film, with Xu Kunwu as consultant, Li Changjian as screenwriter, and Li Li, Wei Daoming, Li Jizhi, Huang Xin, Sen Liu Kuiyuan and others co-starring. The costumes have been made in Guangzhou. All preparations have been properly arranged, and it is decided to go to Shantou on September 1st to take exterior shots.

Medical News 200

Fushou Pharmacy declared that there are very few special effects drugs for the symptom of spitting blood. Our pharmacy at the mouth of Wangping Street, No. 4, on the Bund, sells "Wan Quan Hemoptysis Capsules," which have the wonderful effect of curing blood diseases. All new and old pulmonary tuberculosis, blood in phlegm, and all symptoms of spitting blood, coughing blood, and intestinal blood, etc., are all effective when used. Therefore, recently, new sales points have been added, such as Ciyun Hall at the East Railway Station in Xuzhou, and Sande Foreign Firm in Wuzhou.

Market News 201

Wang Juncaiyun, a native of Fenghua, Zhejiang, had great ambitions from a young age. At the age of ten, he came to Shanghai to engage in commerce. He initially founded the Rongchangxiang Woolen Goods Store and also engaged in other businesses. He was enthusiastic about public welfare and enjoyed doing good deeds. For example, the founding of the orphanage in his hometown county was largely due to Wang's efforts. He also possessed perseverance in social matters, such as initiating the Joint Association of Business Circles from Various Roads and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association to seek benefits for the Chinese people. Following the painful May Thirtieth Massacre, he vowed not to deal in foreign goods, ceased his business, and returned to his hometown. Now, he came to Shanghai for business and resided at Rongchangxiang, but he suddenly passed away yesterday morning due to a stroke. Relatives, party members, old friends, and acquaintances all deeply lamented his passing.

The Aihua Pharmaceutical Company on Wangping Street announced that the one and only dried vegetable bamboo shoots, a specialty of Yuyao, managed by their company, are clean, fresh, delicious, and beneficial to health. They are the only exquisite side dish for meals in summer and autumn. Now, as the factory celebrates its sixth anniversary, they are giving away gifts such as round fans and picture cards, which will end on the 25th of this month. Therefore, wholesale and retail sales have been even more prosperous than before.

Calligraphy and Painting News 202

The Zeng Li Same School Association announced that Li Ruiqing, a Daoist, was a remnant official of the late Qing Dynasty who was proficient in poetry, calligraphy, and painting. His morals and writing were admired by the world, and his students were all over the country. Unfortunately, five years ago, the Daoist passed away suddenly. Today is the Daoist's sixty-fifth posthumous birthday. Disciples such as Zhang Shanzi, Jiang Wanping Jiang, Su, Zhu Dake, Zhang Daqian, Ma Qizhou, Jiang Yiping, Li Yunhui, Yao Yunjiang, Xu Guanqun, and second-generation disciples such as Lu Yuanding, Wang Lan, and Zhu Peiqin, etc., are specially celebrating at the Ludelin on Beijing Road and collecting the Daoist's posthumous manuscripts for publication.
